<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Saturn</b> is the sixth <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a> and the second-largest in the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Gas_giant" title="Gas giant">gas giant</a> with an average radius about nine times that of <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radius_ref_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Radius_ref-12">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Radius_ref_2_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Radius_ref_2-13">[11]</a></sup> It has only one-eighth the average density of Earth, but with its larger volume Saturn is over 95 times more massive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mass_ref_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mass_ref-14">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mass_ref_2_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mass_ref_2-15">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mass_ref_3_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mass_ref_3-16">[14]</a></sup> Saturn is named after the <a href="/wiki/Roman_mythology" title="Roman mythology">Roman</a> <a href="/wiki/Saturn_(mythology)" title="Saturn (mythology)">god of agriculture</a>; its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astronomical_symbol" title="Astronomical symbol">astronomical symbol</a> (♄) represents the god's <a href="/wiki/Sickle" title="Sickle">sickle</a>.</p>
<p>Saturn's interior is probably composed of a core of <a href="/wiki/Iron%E2%80%93nickel_alloy" title="Iron–nickel alloy">iron–nickel</a> and rock (<a href="/wiki/Silicon" title="Silicon">silicon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a> compounds). This core is surrounded by a deep layer of <a href="/wiki/Metallic_hydrogen" title="Metallic hydrogen">metallic hydrogen</a>, an intermediate layer of <a href="/wiki/Liquid_hydrogen" title="Liquid hydrogen">liquid hydrogen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liquid_helium" title="Liquid helium">liquid helium</a>, and finally a gaseous outer layer. Saturn has a pale yellow hue due to <a href="/wiki/Ammonia" title="Ammonia">ammonia</a> crystals in its upper atmosphere. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrical_current" title="Electrical current">Electrical current</a> within the metallic hydrogen layer is thought to give rise to Saturn's planetary <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">magnetic field</a>, which is weaker than Earth's, but has a <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_moment" title="Magnetic moment">magnetic moment</a> 580 times that of Earth due to Saturn's larger size. Saturn's magnetic field strength is around one-twentieth of Jupiter's.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mag_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-mag-17">[15]</a></sup> The outer <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">atmosphere</a> is generally bland and lacking in contrast, although long-lived features can appear. <a href="/wiki/Wind_speed" title="Wind speed">Wind speeds</a> on Saturn can reach 1,800 km/h (1,100 mph), higher than on Jupiter, but not as high as those on <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Science_Ch._2004_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Science_Ch._2004-18">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>The planet's most famous feature is its prominent <a href="/wiki/Rings_of_Saturn" title="Rings of Saturn">ring system</a> that is composed mostly of ice particles, with a smaller amount of rocky debris and <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_dust" title="Cosmic dust">dust</a>. At least 62 <a href="/wiki/Moons_of_Saturn" title="Moons of Saturn">moons</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> are known to orbit Saturn, of which 53 are officially named. This does not include the hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Moonlet" title="Moonlet">moonlets</a> in the rings. <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a>, Saturn's largest moon, and the second-largest in the Solar System, is larger than the planet <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(planet)" title="Mercury (planet)">Mercury</a>, although less massive, and is the only moon in the Solar System to have a substantial atmosphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Titan_ref_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Titan_ref-20">[18]</a></sup></p>
